On the incision of extremities and the sawing of bones.
Extremities can rot either due to intrinsic or extrinsic causes, or when you have treated that corruption with healing medicines and the healing does not occur, or you see the corruption spreading towards the limb without any apparent cause, then you must incise that limb where the corruption has reached, so that the patient may avoid death or severe damage which is a greater detriment to the limb.
And the sign of one to whom this occurs is that the limb turns black as if it had been burned, or it rots near the blackness until that rot spreads to the limb and takes over the whole body; and then you should quickly incise it.
Similarly, if the cause of the corruption is the bite of some venomous creature such as a sea scorpion, viper, spider, or similar.
And if the corruption or the bite is on the fingertip, then you should incise the finger and not give the corruption space to spread to the hand.
Similarly, if it reaches the hand, then you should incise it at the root of the wrist, and not give the corruption space to reach the arm.
And if it invades further, then you should incise the arm at the elbow joint.
And if the corruption passes beyond and you see it around the elbow, then the patient’s death is imminent; administering another cure is only a matter of grace.
Similarly, for the foot, when corruption invades the toe, you should incise it up to one of the joints.
And if it reaches the instep of the foot, then you should incise the entire foot. But if it rises to the knee, then you should incise the leg up to the knee joint.
And if the corruption has already reached the knee, then there is no skill left but resignation, and to leave the patient to death.
And the way to incise the limb or to saw it is that you tighten the bandage on the part below where you want to incise, and tighten another bandage above the location; and the assistant should extend a bandage to the lower parts, and another assistant should extend a bandage upwards; and you separate the flesh that is between the two bandages in a broad space until all the flesh is exposed; and then incise or saw it.
And it is necessary to place linen cloth all around so that it does not touch the healthy part, and that the patient receives a proper bandage and careful dressing.
But if bleeding occurs while you are working, then you should quickly cauterize the location, or place some powders to staunch the blood; and then return to your treatment until it is complete.
And then tie the wounded limb with a bandage at a suitable place, and treat it until it is healed.
And I will recount to you what happened to a man with his foot, this very same incident which I have recounted to you, which is that blackness occurred on his foot with a burning that seemed like a fire burn.
And that corruption first occurred on his toe until it spread to his whole foot.
And then that man prepared himself, seeing that the treatment was progressing to the limb with the severity of what he found of pain and burning, and he incised that foot up to the joint, and he was healed.
A long time later, the same corruption occurred on the finger of his hand.
And then he came to me, and I was compelled to counteract that superfluity with what I placed on his hand of medicines, after cleaning his body; and the superfluity was not counteracted and began to spread to the other finger until it started on the hand.
And he asked me to incise his hand, and I did not want to do it, hoping for the counteraction of that superfluity, and more because I feared the death of the patient from the incision of his hand, as his strength was severely diminished.
And after he despaired of me, he returned to his land and it came to me that that man prepared and incised his whole hand, and he was healed.
And I have included this story only to help with understanding this disease, and to be an example for which it may be recognized and according to which one should act.
On the treatment of sinuses and the quality of irrigation with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it collects pus, and then it is ruptured and perforated, and the pus is released from it, and the place remains empty almost as if it were a vessel, and the membrane over it is like a fine cloth, and it has not progressed to deep corruption, and it does not impinge upon the bone or nerve or ligament, it is called a sinus, and it is not named a fistula.
But if the space is prolonged until the corruption presses on some member, then it is called a fistula and not a sinus.
And the treatment for it is to incise that entire membrane as it is twisted, and especially when it is thin and is like cloth, and make sure that it does not adhere to the place due to its corruption.
But if you expect the membrane to adhere and that the corruption has not yet achieved deep progression, and the membrane has a clear space, then you treat it with irrigation.
And this is what you do: consider the sinus, and if it is large and the discharge is of a fetid odor, then irrigate it with an Egyptian medicine made of oil and sour wine and ginger in equal parts, and place them in a vessel, and cook them over the fire until the medicine turns red and takes on the consistency of honey.
Then you take from it what is necessary and dissolve it with water and honey; and irrigate the sinus with it, and tighten the opening of it, and leave the medicine in it for about two hours.
Then expel it with pressure; and do this for several days until the sinus is cleansed and the odor is gone.
Sometimes, the sinus is irrigated with ash water when this medicine is not available; you take vine ash and put it in water; then strain it and irrigate the sinus with it until you are sure that the sinus is cleared.
If the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then irrigate with water and honey mixed with crushed ginger, and irrigate with wine and honey mixed, because the property of honey is to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the sinus adhere, especially when the wine has an excess of astringency and dryness.
And when you do this several times and you are sure that the sinus is gone, then irrigate it with something that makes flesh grow in it.
And this is done by taking some dyafinicon ointment and dissolving it with rose oil and astringent wine; or you irrigate it with some medicines and other ointments that have the properties which I have already written in the treatise on ointments.
And if the opening of the sinus is narrow so that the irrigation cannula cannot enter, then you gradually widen it with an iron instrument, and place a reed wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened.
Similarly, if the opening is wide, then you sew the edges together and leave a small amount of space for the irrigation cannula without addition.
And if the opening from which the discharge flows is elevated above, then drain it from the lowest point that is in it so that the discharge flows downwards, because when the discharge is confined in the depth of the sinus, flesh will not grow in it.
And if it is not possible for you to drain the sinus from the lower edge of the bone as you wish, then you must prepare the member with a preparation through which the discharge flows lightly as is prepared by you, and that no cause of the discharge is retained in it.
But the one that is over the opening of the sinus, you remove at all times so that it can expel what is lodged in it from the discharge. And so you know if what flows from it from the discharge is much or little, or is digested, or is undigested.
And also you consider the location of that sinus, if the patient feels pain in it or not, and if there is an abscess in it.
And when your treatment is prolonged in such a manner, and you see the matter that is thrown on the opening of the sinus already adhering, or is starting to adhere, then in the morning you untie it or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, then change the cloth for another and renew the ointment.
But if from the sinus after a long time a subtle discharge still comes out, then do not despair of its adherence, because the healing of it is approaching, for there are some people in whom the generation of flesh in their wounds is slow, and in those, the opposite is true.
And if from the sinus for many days undigested discharge has come out, then know that the sinus does not adhere; and if the adherence of the sinus is delayed and the cause is prolonged, then you add to the drying of the medicines, and if the medicines are moist in their substance and in their virtue, they are dry as dyafinicon ointment, when it is added to it with the excess of wax.
And the last thing with which it is treated is that you take dyafinicon ointment and dissolve it in rose oil, and pour over it aged wine equal in its substance, and mix it with it, and use that.
And do similarly in that action, when there is no discharge, dyafinicon ointment, honey cooked until it thickens, and use that; or take myrrh and aloes and incense, crush all and powder it over the honey when it is on the fire, and then spread that on a cloth and press it over the sinus; and spread that with the honey you have cooked until it thickens, and powder it over the cloth and press it.
And sometimes it is treated with long aristolochia and roots of heavenly lily (that is, heavenly lily) and flour of iris and centaury, and use these simply or mixed, crush them and sift and powder them over the honey which I have mentioned; and use that.
And if the sinus is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption is in its depth, and already seek it in the bones or other hard members or ligaments; then treat it with fistular treatment, as mentioned above.
On the treatment of panarici and damaged nails, and the incision of extra fingers and their removal.
A panarici is an abscess that forms under the nail of the thumb or toe and quickly appears on other fingers. When it persists and its treatment is neglected, or when it is caused by a hot abscess or becomes corrupted, it discharges pus that corrodes the root of the nail, quickly destroying the entire nail, often reaching the bone and causing a foul odor. This makes the end of the finger swollen, and the color turns dark.
So, when you have treated it with the method we described earlier and it does not respond to the treatment, you must then cut away all the remaining nail with an iron instrument and then cauterize the wound thoroughly because cauterization is very beneficial in such cases.
But if the bone is healthy and the nail is intact, and the edges of the nail press into the surrounding flesh causing pain and injury, you must place a thin wedge under the edge of the nail that presses on the flesh, push it up, and easily cut that flesh. Apply corrosive burning medicines to the remaining flesh until it is all removed, then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
But if the corruption has already reached the bone, you must cut and remove the affected bone, for it will never heal as long as the bone remains corrupted.
And if you see the corruption and decay spreading in the finger, you must cut it at one of the joints as previously indicated and then treat it until it is healed.
But if the nail is injured by a blow or friction and causes severe pain, you must initially bleed the patient, then cut the nail with a sharp blade in a transverse section from top to bottom. Be careful not to cut into the flesh beneath the nail, as this will cause the patient intense pain and will lead to the growth of excess flesh in the area. Then treat the area with something that relieves pain.
An extra finger, which some people are born with on their hands, is often entirely fleshy, sometimes contains bones, or is sometimes found on the nail.
Some of these are born at the root of the joint, or they may originate from some joints of the fingers. But those that are born on the finger joints are usually not harmful, while those on the joints are more troublesome.
For those that are purely fleshy, the removal is easy: you simply cut it at its root with a broad blade.
But for those that originate from the root of the joint, the treatment is difficult; therefore, be cautious in removing them.
For those born on the finger near the joints, you must first cut the flesh with a circular incision down to the bone, then saw through the bone with a suitable saw, and then treat it until it heals.
But the fusion that occurs between the fingers sometimes by birth, by healing of a wound, by burning, or similar causes, you must cut through that fusion until the fingers return to their natural form.
Then place linen cloth soaked in rose oil between them so they do not easily re-fuse, and keep them separated, or place a thin lead sheet between them until they heal properly.
Similarly, if fusion occurs between some fingers and the palm, cut through the fusion according to the shape and configuration of the member.
On the incision of varices, which are varicose veins.
Varices, also known as varicose veins, are large, twisted veins filled with melancholic superfluities. They often appear in many parts of the body, but are most common in the legs, especially in people who travel, labor, or carry heavy loads.
Thus, it is necessary to purge the body of black bile occasionally with strong expulsion, and then bleed the patient from the basilic vein.
However, their treatment with iron is done in two ways: one involves making an incision and drawing out the black blood, and the other involves lifting and removing the entire vein.
The incision is done in this manner: first, soak the leg with hot water until the thick blood, which is thickened in the leg, is dissolved. Then, tightly bind the leg of the patient from the upper part of the thigh down to below the knee with a bandage. Next, make an incision in the vein at one or two or three places with a broad cut, and draw out the black blood with your hand from the lower part of the leg upward and from the top downward, until the desired amount of blood is extracted and you see that it is enough to relieve the patient.
Then, bandage the area and instruct the patient to abstain from foods that generate black bile.
Repeat the treatment by phlebotomy whenever the veins are filled and it troubles the patient.
But lifting the veins is done in this way: shave the patient's leg if it has many hairs, then put it in a bath and soak the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins become prominent. Alternatively, have the patient perform vigorous exercise if a bath is not available, until the limb is heated.
Then, make an incision in the skin over the vein with a long cut either behind the knee or lower down near the heel.
Next, open the skin with hooks and strip the vein from all sides until it is fully visible, and you see it turning dark red to black.
Then, when you see it and the surrounding tissue looks white like a cord.
Next, insert a rod under it to lift it and detach it from the surrounding tissue, then suspend it with a hook.
Then make another incision about three fingers' width from the first, and strip the skin from the upper part of the vein until it is exposed.
Next, lift the vein and cut it at the lower incision near the heel, then extract and lift it until it comes out through the second incision, and continue extracting it from the upper incisions.
Continue this process until you have extracted it from the highest incision, until the entire vein is removed, and then cut it.
If you have difficulty extracting and lifting it, insert a needle with strong double thread and tie it off, then extract it, or insert the rod underneath and twist your hand around it until it is removed. Be careful not to cut it; if it breaks, it will be very difficult to lift and will cause harm to the patient.
Once you have removed it completely, place a cloth soaked in wine, rose oil, and regular oil over the wound and treat it until it heals.
If the vein is contracted and twisted, and has loops at parts, and is not straight as described, you must make incisions over each twisted part and at the loops, then suspend it with hooks until you can lift it entirely.
Be careful during the incisions not to cut or injure the vein, as it will be difficult to lift; use your skill and prudence.
Shape of the tool used for vein sectioning:
It is not sharpened like a hook, nor does it have a pointed end so that it does not harm the vein; and it has a thick, flexible body, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein due to its thinness; rather, it has an excessive thickness as we have said.
On the extraction of a vein from the leg.
This vein is found in the legs in hot regions such as Ategi in the land of the Arabs and in the hot and dry lands of India, where little soft tissue exists and no grass or trees grow.
It is also easily found in other parts of the body besides the legs.
Its formation is due to putrefaction under the skin, just as snakes, worms, and scarabs form within the body between the skin and the flesh.
A sign of its presence is a severe inflammation in the leg, followed by blistering at the site, and then the vein begins to emerge from the blistered area like a root from a plant.
When the tip appears, wrap a piece of lead weighing one or two drachms around it, and let the lead hang from the leg.
Each time a part emerges, wrap it with lead and tie it off. If it is very long, make an incision in part of it and wrap the rest. Do not cut it close to the root until it is fully out, as cutting it too early will cause it to retract into the flesh, leading to abscess, rot, and a bad ulcer.
Thus, it should be treated gently and extracted little by little until it is completely out, leaving nothing behind in the body.
In some men, this vein has reached a length of five, ten, or even twenty palms.
If it is incised during treatment, insert the rod into the wound and puncture it along the length of the body until all the material is evacuated. Treat the area for a few days with medicines that counter putrefaction, then heal it as you would an abscess.
Sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot or in the foot itself, where it emerges through many openings, with each opening giving rise to a branch.
Treat it as described above, following the steps mentioned.
On the cutting over worms generated under the skin, known as bovine disease.
This disease is called the "bovine disease" in some lands because it often affects cattle. It is a small worm that grows between the skin and the flesh, traveling throughout the body, moving up and down, and can be felt as it moves from limb to limb until it breaks through the skin and comes out.
Its generation is due to the putrefaction of certain humors, just like worms, serpents, and roundworms in the intestines.
It is feared for its malignancy, as when it travels through the body and reaches the head, it can quickly penetrate the eye and destroy it, which happens frequently.
Therefore, when you want to treat and remove it, it can only be done by tracking its movement and feeling it. Then, tightly bind the area above and below it, make an incision over it, and extract it.
If it is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, use a cautery iron to burn the area until it dies. The main concern is its corruption, which can damage the area as mentioned.
If it reaches the head near the eye, bind the area above the eyebrow tightly, make an incision over it, and extract it. The patient should then cleanse their body with medicines that expel putrid humors and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
Regarding the section on the illness called nafir.
This illness is called nafir in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs, and is often transferred from limb to limb.
And I have seen that according to what I will tell you. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and I uncovered her arm and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm, and after an hour, I saw that swelling move as if a worm was climbing up, but more lightly than could be, as if it were quicksilver running from place to place.
And then the pain moved from that place and settled in the muscle, and stayed there for about an hour.
And then it ran through the body until it reached the other arm.
And then she recounted to me that it revolved throughout her entire body as I saw; and I was very amazed by the movement and the speed from limb to limb. And I had already seen this before with my own eyes in that manner, but I have seen many cases where the pain was transferred from limb to limb. But I did not see this with my eyes as I did in the woman.
And I do not think this is anything but because the woman was old, with a dry body and exposed veins, and in this way, that moving swelling appeared to the senses.
And it is necessary that this does not appear according to this back-and-forth movement in those who are healthy and have moist bodies with hidden veins.
And when you want the cure for this, and the patient feels that pain, then it is not apparent to you by sight as we have said, then you press on it and gently shake it until that trapped swelling comes out, and cauterize the spot.
But if you do not see it with your eyes, then you cure it with exercise of the body and with things that expel swellings, and treat them with foul-smelling pills and with serapic pills and the like.
Regarding the extraction of arrows.
Arrows are varied according to their types, and according to the places in the bodies where they strike, because their diversity is such that some have large points, and small, and concave, and blunt, which means solid; and among them are those with three edges, and those with barbs; and those with splinters.
And the signs of the brain are when the arrow strikes there, and it pierces the bone, and it comes out from the covering that is over the brain, because it happens with sudden vehemence, and dizziness, and vertigo, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding and vomiting of bile, and very soon speech is cut off and the voice is destroyed, and from the place of the wound comes out white moisture resembling dust, and something comes out that looks like the moisture of the flesh.
And so if these signs appear to you, then you refrain from the treatment and the extraction of the arrow, unless it is outside.
But the signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and it feels as if it is stuck in a hard place, and not an empty place; and very soon the movement of the arrow is like the movement of the pulse, and from the wound flows black blood, and follows coldness of the extremities, and cold sweat, and fainting; and then you know that death descends without any doubt.
And the signs when the arrow has wounded the lung are the spitting of foamy blood from the wound, and the vessels near the neck are swollen, and the color of the patient is changed, and they exhale with a great noise, and demand the attraction of cold air.
And if the arrow strikes the covering that is in the chest, and the pain then is near the lower ribs, and a great swelling is made with vehement pain and sighing, and not all the muscle members are harmed.
And if the arrow strikes the stomach, then very soon from the wound comes out some undigested food.
And if the arrow strikes the abdomen, and is stuck there, some contents of the wound come out, or the membrane, or the intestine which is ruptured, and there is no hope in the cure by extracting the arrow.
And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine comes out, and something passes to the external parts, and very soon there is pain over the patient, then you know it is mortal.
But the other members like the face, the neck, and the throat, and the shoulders and the arm, and the vertebrae of the back, and the collarbone, and the thigh, and the leg, and their similar members, are saved according to the major conditions when the arrow does not find a vein or artery and is not a poisonous arrow.
And I will recount this to you what I have seen about these arrows, so that you may know about your treatment.
Which case is, because in a man, an arrow struck in the tear duct of his eye in the root of the nose, and I extracted it from the other side, under the cartilage of his ear, and he was healed, and no harm occurred to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from a Jew which struck him in the cartilage of his eye, under the lower eyelid, and the arrow was already hidden and only a small tip with which it was attached to the shaft was obtained, and it was a large arrow from the sharp arrows of the Turks, with iron tip that did not have barbs.
And the Jew was healed, and no harm occurred to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from a Christian man which had struck his throat, and it was an Arabic arrow, and it had barbs; and so I cut over it between two guides, and it was already submerged in his throat; and then I delicately worked with it, and soon I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
And I extracted another arrow from a man which had struck his abdomen, and I thought he would die from it; and then, after thirty days had passed and nothing had changed in his condition, I cut over the arrow and worked on it, and he was healed, and no bad accident happened to him.
And I saw another man in whom an arrow struck his back, and the wound healed over it, and after nearly seven years, the arrow emerged at the root of his thigh.
And I saw a woman in whom an arrow struck her abdomen, and the wound healed inside, and nothing changed in her condition, and the woman found no harm in any of her natural functions.
And I saw another man in whom an arrow struck his face and the wound healed over it and the arrow remained, finding no pain there, and many similar cases to these.
And I extracted an arrow from the man of the prince of the king which had struck the middle part of his nose and had already shifted a little to the right side, and the whole arrow was hidden.
And I was called to the treatment of him soon after the arrow struck within three days.
And then I found the wound from the arrow very narrow; and then I examined it with a fine probe, and I did not feel it; but he felt a prick under his right ear, and then I suspected that the prick was from the tip of the arrow.
And I applied a plaster to the location with an attractive and digestive virtue, trusting that the place would form an abscess so that the location of the arrow would appear to me, and so it could be accessed.
And no significant accident occurred at the location indicating that the arrow had reached that place; and I continued with the plaster on it for many days and no accident occurred; and the wound healed meanwhile, and the patient remained without extraction for many days until one day he felt the arrow in his nose and reported it to me.
And then I applied a sharp corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it was opened, and with a probe, I examined it, and I found the fine tip of the arrow, which was attached to the shaft.
And then I continued applying the medicine to the opening of the wound until the tip of the arrow appeared visibly to me, and I spent time on this for a period of four months.
And then, after the wound was enlarged, and it was possible for me to insert the forceps into it and remove it, and if it did not obey extraction, then I did not cease to handle and work on it with various techniques, until one day I started using techniques to grasp it with properly made forceps, according to the form that will come at the end of the chapter, until I extracted it; and then I restored the wound.
And some doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored, and I restored it and the wound healed, and the patient was completely healed, and it did not harm him in any way.
And I recount to you the quality of the extraction of some arrows so that you set a rule and understanding about what I have not said, because the parts of this art and its definitions are not comprehended with narration nor do they comprehend the book.
And the wise practitioners compare little over much; and from what is present over what is absent; and find new operations and new instruments for the descent of the external causes of the art when it happens.
And so I say that arrows are not extracted from the limbs where they are stuck except in two ways: either by pulling from the place where they entered; or by the opposite side.
And the one that is extracted from the place where it entered, it is an arrow stuck in a fleshy place, and it is pulled and extracted.
And if it does not obey extraction from the hour it struck, then you must leave it for some days until the flesh around it decays, and the extraction and egress are eased.
And similarly, if it is stuck in bone and does not obey extraction, then leave it for some days and repeatedly pull and move it each day, and then it will be extracted.
And if it does not obey extraction after some days, then you must perforate around the arrow in that bone on all sides with a fine drill until the place around the arrow is enlarged, and then extract it.
But if the arrow is already hidden in the body, and hidden from sensation, then you search for it with a probe, and if you feel it, then pull it with some instruments that are suitable for its extraction.
And if you cannot manage it because of the constriction of the wound and the length of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein there, then you work on the wound until it is enlarged and it is possible to extract the arrow.
And if it has barbs by which it is held, then you release the flesh in which it is stuck on all sides with all the skill you can manage; and work on it, if you cannot manage the evasion of the flesh with the fracture of the barbs and their twisting until it obeys.
And when you manage the extraction of the arrow in any place where it is, then you use twisting of your hand with forceps on all sides until it obeys; and work with utmost subtlety so that the arrow is not broken and its extraction is not made difficult for you.
And if you cannot manage it at that time, then you leave it for a few days until the parts around it decay, and then work on it again because then it will be eased. But if you encounter a flow of blood, then you manage it as we have discussed in its chapter.
And guard your skill from cutting a vein or nerve, or tendon, and manage it with every technique you can for the evasion of the arrow; and do this with ease and tranquility and slowness and firmness as I have recounted to you.
And so you contract the arrow so that the patient is according to the shape according to which it was when the arrow struck him, because it is more helpful. But if this is not possible for you, then you manage with what is possible for you with the shapes.
But the arrows that are extracted by the opposite side, or where some part of it already protrudes outward, or the tip of the arrow causes swelling by sensation of the part above the close flesh and sometimes that part is prominent; then you cut over it; and the cutting should be according to the quantity that the forceps can grasp; and then you pull it, because it is made easier to extract.
But if it is held in the bone, then you twist the blade counter to the way until the arrow presses into the bone, and enlarges itself, and then extract it.
And if not, leave it for some days, and then work on it until it comes out.
And if the shaft of the arrow is in it, then you push it with it.
But if the shaft is broken and you want to push, then you insert into it, if it is broken, a concave instrument so that it fits into the concavity of the arrow's tail and then push it with it.
But if the arrow is concave, then you push it with a strong instrument inserted into it, because the arrow is eased by it.
And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must excise all the flesh where the poison is, if this is possible for you, and then treat it with what is appropriate.
And if the arrow falls in the chest, or in the abdomen, or in the bladder, or in the side, and is close enough for you to touch it with the probe, and it is possible for you to cut over it, then cut over it and guard against cutting a vein or nerve, and extract it, and then sew the wound if needed, and treat it until it is healed.
The form of forceps with which the arrows are extracted:
Let their ends be like a bird's beak which are made with a saw so that they do not let go of the arrow.
And many types of these are made, large, small, and medium, according to the size of the arrow and its thinness, and the width of the wound, and its constriction.
like a ray so that the insertion of it into the concave arrow is eased and it is pushed with it.
Of phlebotomy of the veins.
The veins for phlebotomy from which the usual places to perform it are as follows: two pulsating veins near the ears, called alhasisain; two veins in the temples; two veins in the tear ducts of the eyes called aspicientz; a vein in the middle of the forehead; a vein at the tip of the nose; two veins at the neck; two veins in the upper lip; two veins in the lower lip; — these are the veins called algelic —; and two veins under the tongue. But the veins that are phlebotomized in the arms are five: One of these is the cephalic vein, which is on the outer side; and people call it "the head vein," also known as the middle vein, composed of a branch of the basilic vein and another branch of the cephalic vein; people call this "the vein of the whole body," and the basilic vein is on the inner side, known as “citillar,” called by common people "the vein of the belly"; the funis of the arm, located over the elbow, is the one where phlebotomy is performed, appearing over the pulse by clear manifestation; and salvatella, which is the vein between the ring finger and the little finger, located in two branches.
In the foot and leg, there are three veins; one is under the curve of the knee on the outer side; the second is the saphenous vein, located under the leg on the inner side; and the sciatic vein, located under the leg on the outer side; in the leg, there are other veins similar to these.
The benefit of the veins near the ears is for old catarrhs and migraines and scurf and old head ulcers.
The method of bleeding these veins is as I tell you: shave the head of the patient, and rub the back of the patient's head where both veins are with a large cloth with good friction; then tighten the patient's neck with a band until the two veins and their places appear near the ears at two pressed places on the head; and find them with your finger, and if you feel their pulse with your finger, mark the spot with a probe.
Then take the lancet knife, which is for incision, and insert it under the vein in the skin until the phlebotomy reaches the bone. Then lift your hand with the vein and the skin upwards and incise the vein with an incision knife. And let the length of the incision be the width of two fingers joined or around that; and let as much blood flow out as you want.
Then press it with powders and leave it until it is healed.
And it is already mentioned at the beginning of the book the incision of these and their cauterization.
But for the two arterial veins in the temples, the benefit of phlebotomy is for chronic and severe migraines, persistent ophthalmia, and acute excessive discharges from the eyes.
And the method to phlebotomize them is as I tell you: have the patient tighten their neck greatly until the two veins appear by sensation through clear manifestation and their pulse is felt under your finger; then mark with a probe.
Then lift the skin above the vein upwards with your index finger, insert the incision phlebotomy tool underneath, lift the vein upwards; and incise it as you did with the other two veins; and let the blood flow according to the amount you need.
Then loosen the patient's constriction, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton and powders on it and press it tightly, and leave it until it is healed.
And the remembrance of them, and their incision, and the extraction is already mentioned at the beginning of the book.
And thus the benefit of phlebotomy of the forehead vein is similar to the phlebotomy of the cephalic vein for chronic facial diseases and migraines and redness and foul ulcers.
And the method of phlebotomy there is as I tell you; that is, the patient tightens their neck with a band until the vein appears; then take the instrument called fossori of which this is its form:
Place the prominent point which is at the head of the fossori on that vein and strike it with a hammer or other object in that manner, and let the blood flow as much as you want; then loosen the patient's constriction and press it until it is healed.
And sometimes it is opened with a wide phlebotomy tool, but the phlebotomy tool should not be of sharp extremity like the other phlebotomy tools, rather it should be of wide extremity, and phlebotomize it transversely, because the bone is close and it would easily break the phlebotomy tool if it is fine.
But the benefit of the two veins in the tear ducts of both eyes is for scab in the eyes, redness, and inflammation in the eyes, and facial diseases.
And the method of phlebotomy is that the patient tightens their neck with a band, then phlebotomize those, and you stand over the patient's head.
And perform the phlebotomy transversely a little with a small phlebotomy tool, because there is no flesh in that area; and if the phlebotomy tool is fine, its extremity will break easily.
And then let the blood flow as much as you need, place cotton on them, and press them for one night, and then loosen them.
But the phlebotomy of the vein of the nose is beneficial for acute fever and sudden severe fever, facial diseases, migraines, and redness that occur on the face, especially when chronic.
And the method of phlebotomy there is that the patient tightens their neck and you hold their nose with your left hand, take the fine long phlebotomy tool and insert it in the middle of the nose tip straightly, because the vein does not appear by sensation there, and because the blood starts to flow immediately.
You should gradually withdraw your hand with the phlebotomy tool and let the blood flow according to your need; then bind it for one night, because it heals quickly.
But the benefit of phlebotomy of the two guidegui veins is for nasal constriction, the onset of leprosy, many diseases, impetigo, and corrosive ulcers like herpes.
And the method of phlebotomy for those is that the patient tightens below each vein in their neck with a band; the practitioner should stand over the patient's head, and the patient should sit on a chair.
Then phlebotomize the vein lengthwise with a wide phlebotomy tool little by little; then extract blood in a moderate amount or according to what is necessary for that; then do the same with the other vein.
Then loosen the band and press the two veins with moderate pressure so that the patient is not suffocated, and leave it until the morning because the wound is healed.
And the benefit of phlebotomy of the algelic veins is for small abscesses and pustules of the mouth, gum decay, bad ulcers, and fissures, and bad ulcers in the nose and its surrounding area.
And the method of phlebotomy for those is that you make the patient sit in front of you, tighten their neck with a band, then turn their lips and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left side; and the identification of each is by the blackness of each of both, and more so because around them are small black veins; then incise each with an incision tool.
But if you have doubt, and do not know which one it is, then you should proceed to incise the largest of those, and the most apparent of those.
And do the same with the two veins in the upper lips.
But the benefit of the phlebotomy of the two veins under the tongue is similar to the phlebotomy of the cephalic vein for inflammations in the throat, diseases of the uvula, and mouth diseases.
And the method of phlebotomizing those is that you hold the patient between your hands facing the sun, lift their tongue, and look under the tongue, from one side to the other, and the color of each is leaning towards blackness.
And then phlebotomize each; and be careful not to keep your hand too long in phlebotomizing those, because there are arteries underneath them.
And the veins that are phlebotomized in the elbow are the ones where blood usually flows in all men, and their phlebotomy is done in two ways, either puncture with the myrtle or olive phlebotomy tool with a declining subtlety; or cut with a knife-like phlebotomy tool, called alnessil, and this is its form:
it is wide like some, and suitable for opening concave veins that are visibly large, and for those that contain thick, turbid blood.
And this phlebotomy tool is narrower and has a finer tip, and is suitable for phlebotomy of fine veins that contain fine, yellowish blood.
But the benefit of the phlebotomy of the basilic vein, which is one of three veins, is that it extracts the blood from the diseases that are below the throat and neck, and from what follows to the chest and abdomen.
And it is necessary for the phlebotomist, when performing that phlebotomy, to be very careful and cautious because there is an artery underneath, and if he makes a mistake and hits the artery with the phlebotomy tool, it will cause blood flow, so he should not phlebotomize it with a puncturing tool, but rather cut with the alnessil.
And if the basilic vein does not appear clearly, then you should leave it and move to another, or look for one of its branches; or phlebotomize in the place at the end of the arm, because it is visible; and cut it with the alnessil phlebotomy tool as we have said.
But if you want to perform the phlebotomy yourself, then you should first tighten the arm and find the pulse point, then mark it with ink; and then bind the arm and cut the vein with a concave incision with the alnessil phlebotomy tool as we have said; and be careful not to let the cut fall in the area of the artery.
And when you see, while tightening the binding, swelling in the place you marked with ink, that swelling is from the artery, and then you should avoid it.
And if you see the blood flow in the phlebotomy like the urine of a child, and the blood is thin and red, then you know it is arterial blood; and then you should quickly place your finger over it for a long time; and then remove your finger, and if the blood stops, because often it does, then you should bind the arm and leave it.
And protect the patient from movement, be cautious with him and do not disturb him for some days until it is healed.
But if the blood does not stop, and you see that you do not have the necessary medicine, then you cut the artery if it appears; because its end is constricted, and the blood is stopped; or you take the bark of pistachio, prepare it, take one half and press it on the vein with a descending tightness with a bandage and powders until the next day.
And then if the blood stops, good; if not, then treat it with what is previously mentioned about the powders that stop blood flow.
And stopping the blood there is difficult in many cases because of the small area of the wound and the possibility of binding the arm.
But the phlebotomy of the fusca vein benefits by extracting the blood from the upper part of the head and the lower part of the body; because it is composed of a branch of the basilic vein and a branch of the cephalic vein, as we have said.
And it is necessary for the phlebotomist to be cautious when performing phlebotomy on it, because there is a nerve underneath it; and if he punctures with the phlebotomy tool and hits the nerve, it will cause numbness, and its healing is difficult, and it may never heal completely. And this nerve is sometimes felt; and if it is hidden in some people and is thin and not visible, then you should place the phlebotomy tool with which you perform the incision with the alnessil, and avoid the nerve with your skill.
And if the vein is between two nerves, then you make the vein longitudinally.
The benefit of the phlebotomy of the cephalic vein is that it draws blood from the head and is beneficial for diseases of the eyes.
And it is necessary in this one specifically, if you want to phlebotomize it, to use the olive or myrtle phlebotomy tool; because it is the safest of all veins, since there is no artery or nerve underneath it.
But nevertheless, it often becomes inflamed in some people, when it is not phlebotomized with the first percussion, but this inflammation does not harm at all.
The first thing you need to know is that phlebotomy is not administered except in the preservation of health and with the hope and caution of preventing diseases, and that phlebotomy should be done in one of the veins in the elbow, that is: cephalic, fusca, and basilic; and that phlebotomy should be done at the beginning of spring, on an empty stomach in spring and autumn, and in winter after a meal, when there are signs of fullness.
And phlebotomy should be done on the third day or the first after three hours of the day have passed.
But phlebotomy that is administered, when it causes convenience and necessity, whether by night or by day, at any hour and at any time.
And it is necessary that a child is not phlebotomized until they are fourteen years old, and a pregnant woman is not phlebotomized except from the fourth month to the seventh, and the elderly are not phlebotomized who have already passed sixty years.
And when someone wants to be phlebotomized in any manner, it is necessary to cleanse their bowels before the phlebotomy with a leon enema, if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw the impurities in the phlebotomy from the bowels, which are putrid, and do not harm the principal organs.
And patients with excessive nausea and hangover should not be phlebotomized, nor those recovering from illness or drunkenness until it has passed, nor those suffering from dropsy, and phlebotomy should be avoided near colic pain and vomiting, and near bowel conditions, and near excessive coitus and work and exercise from fasting or vigils and any cause that weakens the strength, whether bodily or animal.
And also consider the thinning of humors before this if the blood is thick, with foods and drinks, and with medicines if it is possible to do so.
And take a bath beforehand if no cause prohibits it, or exercise in some way so that the blood is thinned.
And perform the phlebotomy in the morning, that is, around the third hour, as we have said.
And make sure that the patient's peace is guarded on that day from all bad animal accidents, such as anxiety, anger, fear, and all bodily accidents, such as excessive work, pain, coitus, and similar things.
And at their side, have present the things that men usually use with aromaticity and fragrance, and with balm and similar things according to the quantity possible.
And the phlebotomist should sit on a stool that is higher than the stool of the one who is to be phlebotomized.
And then, extend their arm, and the phlebotomist should rub it with their hand two or three times; and then tighten the ligature with a strap and wrap it around twice.
And let the tightness be moderate, because if the tightness is not equal, or if it is too tight, it prevents the flow of blood; or if it is too loose, it prevents the proper flow of blood outward.
And after the tightening, the one who is to be phlebotomized should rub their hands together until the veins are swollen and become visible.
And then the phlebotomist should anoint the phlebotomy tool with a bit of old oil; and then place the index finger of the left hand on the vein, below the spot where the phlebotomy is to be done, so the vein moves slightly, and the tapping ceases because some veins act like a fleeing string towards the phlebotomy, and some are full of air and when you place the phlebotomy tool on them, they contract towards the tool, and the phlebotomist is deceived; and the tool does not open the vein, and if it does, the vein becomes narrow.
And therefore, the phlebotomist must be firm and diligent in all these matters.
And then place the phlebotomy tool, but if the vein is not opened at once, then it is good; otherwise, you should try again a little below that spot, or above it with speed, if the spot is not inflamed.
And if the spot is inflamed, or the patient is scared, then leave it for a day or two, and do not tighten the ligature, as it may quickly attract a cautious inflammation, and do not take a bath.
And then repeat the phlebotomy if it is necessary.
And if the opening is small and the blood flows subtly, and you fear that the quantity of blood desired will not be released, then you should repeat the phlebotomy in that hole with precision and enlarge the opening a little, and do this quickly before the spot becomes inflamed, because the spot becomes inflamed in many people due to a small opening.
But if you see it already inflamed, then do not repeat it there, as there is no reason; and place some portion of the oil bandage on it, as it alleviates the blood flow. And it is better in this case than oil and other oils.
And similarly, administer an oil bandage in every phlebotomy in which you phlebotomize the veins to prevent blood flow, and use this theriac alfadoc and sagzenea when placed on the spot, as the blood becomes thinned and mixed when it is thick.
And if a large abscess forms at the phlebotomy site, which often happens, especially to one who has not been bled before, or if the vein's opening is small, then hurry, and place on the spot a sponge soaked in water and salt, slightly heated, and tighten it for an hour, because it will dissolve.
And it is necessary to do this after the blood has flowed from that vein, with the closure of it or another vein.
And if there remains some darkness or greenness at the spot for a few days, it does not harm; and if you wish, place on it something made of aloe and dissolved myrrh, or something of mint or calamint juice or something similar.
And often abscesses and swellings occur due to phlebotomy of the basilic vein.
And then place your hand on it, and if you find softness under your compression on it, then that swelling is bad and harmful; and then be careful not to place on it any of the things we have mentioned, because it may quickly cause blood to flow from the artery.
And make a plaster with something that has astringency, so that the spot is hardened, and then treat it with other care until it is healed.
And you need to extract blood from everyone according to the amount of their strength and according to the dominant color of the blood as it appears.
Because if the blood is black, then you let it flow until it is red; and similarly, if you see it is thick, then you let it flow until it is thinned; and similarly, if it is sharp, until its sharpness is removed.
And it is necessary for someone who is full and strong and needs a single blood extraction, that the phlebotomy of the vein be enlarged and the opening wide.
And in someone who is frail, do the opposite, and the blood should be extracted in multiple sessions, and the opening should be narrow.
And the best way to administer vein phlebotomy is that the cut be transverse, not punctured.
And this method of phlebotomy is safe from blood flow and nerve incision, and it is more praiseworthy and safer than phlebotomy along latitude and longitude.
And for those prone to fainting from phlebotomy, it is necessary to treat them before phlebotomy with a little bread soaked in pomegranate wine or simple heated oxymel; and extract a little blood in three or four sessions.
And if there is a cold constitution, then before phlebotomy take bread soaked in myrrh syrup or honey syrup flavored with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger and similar, or in a very fragrant aromatic syrup.
And if fainting occurs due to phlebotomy, and it is caused by a lot of blood loss, then it is necessary to drink meat broth and very fragrant subtle syrup; and use aromatic substances with aloe, and rub their chest with it.
And use other remedies that we have mentioned in the section on fainting due to evacuation.
And anyone who wants to vent their arm and dissolve their blood a second time, it is necessary for those whose phlebotomy is for large evacuation, and their strength is weak, to evacuate the blood little by little, that is, according to their strength, in continuous days.
But anyone who wants to vent their arm and expel their blood a second time, and their body is strong, should do this around seven or nine hours after the first phlebotomy.
But anyone who wants to draw blood from their body to the opposite side of the part to which it flows should be vented on the second or third day.
But a body in which there is a lot of blood already heated and acute and causing fever, it is necessary to expel a large amount of blood at once, and the opening should be enlarged until fainting occurs, after you have maintained all the conditions of phlebotomy; and place your hand on the pulse to prevent death instead of fainting, as this often happens when the phlebotomist is ignorant and negligent.
And it is not necessary when you want to untie the arm and evacuate the blood a second time, as the opening of the vein is already closed and the blood flow is difficult, to press on it with force and the bent arm is slightly extended, as this is very bad.
First, leave it until it can be phlebotomized a second time; or remove the coagulated blood at the opening of the vein with the sharpness of the phlebotomy tool; or apply theriac alfarach, or sagzenea on it, and compress it lightly until the blood flows out.
And if the vein is inflamed, then leave it and do not touch it until the inflammation has subsided.
And if you are forced to evacuate the blood a second time, and there is no other option, then you bleed from that spot or from another vein in the other arm.
And the vein called "funis del bras" is phlebotomized instead of the fusca or the basilic vein when they are not found or are hidden, because it is composed of those.
And the quality of the phlebotomy of it is that the patient immerses their hand in warm water until the skin reddens and the vein becomes clearly visible.
And then it should be tightly bandaged with moderate tightness; and then phlebotomize it with a small transverse cut, not longitudinally.
And the opening should be wide and your phlebotomy should be done on the vein a little above the wrist.
And if the blood flow is restricted, then immerse the hand in warm water again and let the blood flow into the water until you achieve the desired amount.
But if it is during the summer, then you are excused from immersing the hand in warm water again, and it is better to immerse the body of the blood in warm water during the winter.
And the phlebotomy of this vein is safer than all other veins because there is no pulsating vein or nerve beneath it.
And the phlebotomy of the right hand’s vein is beneficial for liver diseases.
And the quality of the phlebotomy of it is that you tightly bandage the hand or use your hand, after immersing it in warm water, until the vein is swollen and clearly visible; and then phlebotomize it transversely; and if you cut it completely, it will not harm in any way.
And make sure not to press the hand too much with the phlebotomy tool, because beneath it are the nerves of the fingers stripped of flesh.
And then immerse the hand in warm water again and let the blood flow into it, because if you do not immerse it in warm water again, the blood will coagulate in the opening of the vein and restrict the flow.
And when the blood is extracted according to the needed amount, then apply oil and salt on the vein to prevent it from closing too quickly; and similarly, this should be done on all narrow openings.
But the benefit of the phlebotomy of that of the left hand is that it is beneficial for spleen diseases.
And do similarly in the phlebotomy of it as you did in the other.
And the benefit of the phlebotomy of the saphenous vein is for diseases in the lower part of the body, such as diseases of the uterus, and menstrual retention, and diseases of the kidneys and chronic ulcers of the thighs and legs, and similar diseases.
And the quality of the phlebotomy of it is that the patient immerses their foot in warm water and rubs it until the veins are clearly visible; and bandage above the ankle with a strap; and the location of the vein on the heel is visible towards the big toe, and from it branch many veins on the surface of the foot.
And then phlebotomize the widest branch or below the calf towards the heel towards its junction, as it is better and safer.
And if you phlebotomize it on the surface of the foot, then beware of the nerves beneath it on the surface of the foot, and apply the phlebotomy transversely, almost as if you were cutting it.
And the phlebotomy should be gentle.
But if the blood flow is restricted, then immerse the foot in warm water again and let the blood flow into it until it is evacuated.
And if the phlebotomist makes a mistake the first time, then try again a little higher, as the location is safe; and do not fear harm, but beware of the nerves as we have said.
And similarly do the phlebotomy of the saphenous vein of the other foot equally.
And for the sciatic vein, the location as we have said is towards the heel below the outer ankle.
And the benefit of the phlebotomy of it is for hip pain when it is due to bad blood.
And the quality of the phlebotomy of it is that the patient enters a bath, and quickly and tightly bandages the thigh from the side of the hip down to the heel about four fingers in width with a long, thin bandage, because it is only visible in this way.
And then when it appears, phlebotomize it with whatever tool you can and transversely, as it is better; or cut it by incision or section, as the location is safe.
And it is very hidden in many people; and if you find it, and it is not visible by touch at all, then phlebotomize any branch of it, which is the one that appears on the back of the foot towards the little and ring toes.
And beware of the nerves, and let the blood flow the desired amount.
And then untie the bandage and apply cotton on the phlebotomy site and press the spot, as it heals quickly.
On cupping and the qualities of using them.
Cupping glasses are made of horn, or brass, or glass.
And cupping is done in two ways: one of them is with scarification and blood extraction, and the other is cupping without scarification.
And this cupping without scarification is done in two ways, either with fire or without fire.
And the cupping with scarification and blood extraction is applied to fourteen places on the body, of which one place where cups are applied is the alnocrati, and it is the back part of the head; and the middle part of it on both sides of the neck together; and cupping of the chin below the mandible further below the mouth; and cupping of both shoulder blades; and cupping of the alohoster, which is over the end of the tailbone; and cupping of the two upper arms, which are the two arms; and cupping of both ankles; and cupping of both thighs.
And cupping does not extract blood except from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore does not lose its effectiveness through these, unlike phlebotomy; nor should cupping be done with fire or without fire in any illness caused by repletion until the whole body is evacuated.
But if necessity forces cupping due to illness or continuously, administer it at any time at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, and in the middle of it and at any time.
And then when you see any of those causes, and especially if it is on the third or middle of the month, then we command cupping to be done after two or three hours of the day have passed.
And the benefit of cupping on the nape is that it helps with heaviness in the head and those who are sunken around the eyes; but this should be done after evacuating the whole body.
And this cupping is in the location of the cephalic phlebotomy.
And it is not lawful to use it on someone with a cold complexion, or who has catarrh, because it does great harm to them.
And therefore it should not be used on the elderly, and on those whose heads have cold diseases.
But for those who continue with it, it causes forgetfulness; and therefore you should command the cupper to lightly place their hand with the cup on the lower parts, fearing the generation of forgetfulness.
But cupping of alkehel is in the location of the phlebotomy of the dark and basilic veins: and therefore it helps with asthma, and the constriction of the chest and the splitting of the chest instrument, and cough, and repletion.
And it should be pressed a little, because if placed lower, it causes weakness in the body and stomach.
And the cupping of alhagdahan helps with accidental headaches and ophthalmia, and migraine, and preoccupation, and pains in the roots of the teeth; and it is in the location of the basilic phlebotomy.
And you should command the cupper not to press with the scarification so as not to cut the artery and cause a flow of blood.
And cupping below the chin helps with ulceration in the mouth, and gingival corruption, and similar diseases in the mouth, and it stands in the location of the phlebotomy of the sublingual veins which are in the two lips.
But cupping done on both shoulder blades helps with headache caused by repletion of heat.
And cupping of the two parts inside the thighs helps the phlebotomy of three veins, which are the basilic, dark, and cephalic veins, because it attracts the blood from all those smaller veins in the flesh, and those small veins from the other larger veins until the attraction reaches the three veins.
And command the cupper not to proceed too much with the scarification, because the location is devoid of flesh, and beneath it are nerves and arteries.
And it is a cupping glass with which cupping is done over the sacrum and helps with hemorrhoids of the anus and lower ulcers.
And you should command the cupper to use a large cup, and it should be made of brass, because the location needs strong sectioning; and quickly small cups are placed and scarified with scarification.
But cupping of the legs decreases by clear diminution, because it draws the blood from the whole body, and helps with old pains in the kidneys and uterus, and the bladder; and it provokes menstruation, and helps with swelling and dropsy; and it stands in the location of the phlebotomy of two saphenous veins, and alahorcoben, and both ankles.
However, it greatly weakens the whole body and causes fainting in many people.
And the benefit of cupping alahorcoben is similar to the benefit of cupping both legs.
And the quality of the position of the cups is that you place the cup at first empty and suck with moderate suction, and do not prolong the position of the cups, but place them lightly, and remove them quickly, so that the humors come to the location evenly. And do not stop repeating this and continue until you see the location redden and swell and the redness of the blood appears.
And then you scarify and repeat the suction little by little, and carefully consider the condition of the bodies.
For the person with tender flesh and sparse pores, you should scarify once and no more, so that the location does not become ulcerated.
And command the cupper to make the scarification larger and a little deeper, and adjust the suction with ease.
And if the blood is thick, then scarify twice, because the first time opens the way for thinning the blood and its watery part. But the second time it scrutinizes the acquired extraction of thick blood.
And if the blood is very feculent, then do the scarification a third time to achieve the final result.
And finally, when we want to extract the blood little by little or just a little, one scarification is enough.
And if we want to extract a lot of blood, we scarify with many scarifications; and if we know that the blood is thick, then we should scarify deeply.
And the limit of scarification is just the depth of the skin.
And if that of which the skin is thick, hard, dark, and its pores are tight, the places for the cups should be smeared with softening, opening, and resolving agents; if it is in summer, such as aloe oil or violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or gourd seed oil; and if it is in winter, then narcissus oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or blood oil, and similar ones.
And if the excess is thick and cold, then the oil should be amaranth oil, or balsamite oil, or aloe oil, or dill oil, and similar ones.
But if the cupping patient has wide pores and tender flesh, then they should avoid oil, and it is advisable that the places for the cups near the cupping are washed with rose water or cold water of nightshade, or gourd water, or purslane water, and similar ones.
And those whose blood is very humid should wash the cups with vinegar, or water of myrtle and sumac and similar ones.
And those whose excesses are thick should wash the cups with old wine, or water of savory, which is marjoram, or decoction of dill, or chamomile, and similar ones.
And it is advisable that cupping be done before bathing; beforehand it should be administered near the bath for one or two hours, and it is advisable to sleep near the cupping.
What is it that needs to be regulated for cupping or bloodletting before cupping.
You should consider at the beginning: if the cupping patient or the one who should be bloodletted is choleric and full of acute blood and inflammation, then they should take cooling agents, such as sour pomegranates, and endives with vinegar, and lettuce, and chicory, and julep, and similar ones.
And give them foods such as chickens, and game bird meats, and foods prepared with sour agents, and similar ones.
And for those whose complexion is cold, they should drink syrup of honey, or syrup of chicory seeds, and sumac, and very fragrant wine mixed between old and new; and it is recommended that they use little to drink and eat, and give them foods such as chickens, and partridges, and pigeons, and small birds.
And it is advisable that on the day of cupping and bloodletting the drink is more than the food.
And it is advisable to give at some hours to some people to drink theriac alpharac, or musk medicines, that is nutmeg, or alcelite before cupping or before bloodletting or nearby, so that the principal members are strengthened and the blood is thinned; and they should not take it heated.
But the cups without scarification are placed on the liver, and on the spleen and gout, and on the navel, on the knee joints, and the hip, because these members do not tolerate scarification on themselves.
And it is not intended for those except to attract blood from the member, as we place a cup on the breast in the disease of blood flow from the nose; and we use it to dissolve cold viscosity of the member, as we place it on the belly and navel; because it thins the member and warms it and removes the pain because it resolves wind.
And it is placed on the kidneys when obstruction or pus occurs in them, because by the virtue of strong attraction it quickly opens the obstruction and eradicates the pus from its place.
And similarly it acts when placed on the liver and spleen against wind enclosed in them.
And these cups are administered empty with suction only; and sometimes they are administered with fire.
And sometimes they are administered filled with warm water in diseases of the spleen.
And this is so that the cup is filled and is larger, that is hot water alone or water in which herbs suitable for this are cooked.
The form of the cup administered with fire: let the opening be two fingers wide, as we have formed it; and the depth be half a palm; and let it be on the side of it, in the place that is in the circuit, half of it, the hole be small as the amount that a needle can enter.
Let it be made of red brass or citrus, with thick edges, smooth, equal, and clean so that it does not harm the member upon its position on it.
And let it be in the middle of it a transverse rod of brass or iron, on which a candle with fire is placed.
And let this cup be much larger than the one we have mentioned; and a little smaller than that according to the diseases and the age of the one who uses it.
And the cups for children and the exhausted are different from the cups for the young and robust bodies.
And the quality of placing this cup with fire on the member is that it stretches the wick with the fire of decent wood in front of a little wax candle, and place it on the middle of the transverse rod in the middle of the cup, so that the fire is lit around the lower part so that the body of the patient is not burned.
And then place it on the member of the patient, and the finger be on the hole that we mentioned, until when we hold the cups and do not need to hold the finger and let the steam out through that hole, then the cup will soon be released.
And ignite the wick properly, and repeat it if necessary.
But in a cup that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, with water, in which there is no transverse rod nor hole, and it is administered only by being filled with water, and it is placed on the member only.
And this is its form: And this cup, the larger it is, the better, so that it can receive a large amount of water.

Leeches are not applied to many parts except to parts where it is not possible to place cups, due to the small size of those parts, such as the feet and gums and similar to them; or on parts devoid of flesh, such as the finger and the nose and similar to them.
And the quality of using those is that you have found leeches in clean freshwater ponds.
And then they should be left for a day and a night in fresh water until they are hungry, and no substance remains in their stomachs; and then the body should be evacuated at the beginning with bloodletting and cupping; and then rub the patient's part until it reddens; and then place them on it.
And when they are filled and fall off.
And if it is possible to suction the place with a cup, it is more beneficial afterwards.
And if not, then wash the place with vinegar and then with plenty of water; and it should be rubbed and squeezed.
And if the blood continues to flow after the leeches fall off, and this happens, then soak a linen cloth in cold water, and place it over it until the bleeding stops.
And if the blood is abundant, then sprinkle over it crushed vitriol, or galls and similar astringents, until the blood stops; or place on the site halves of cooked beans, and leave them until the beans adhere to the site, and the blood stops.
And if necessary, repeat the application of leeches, as often as you can replace them.
And if leeches are prohibited from being suspended, then rub the site with fresh blood or insert a needle into the sites until blood comes out; and then place them, because when they sense any blood, they will attach immediately.
And when you want them to fall off, sprinkle a little crushed aloe, or salt, or ash on them, and they will fall off immediately.
Thus begins the prologue of the third part: on restoration. This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine; it is the restoration of fracture and dislocation incidents in the bones.
Oh, son, know that foolish doctors and laypeople boast of this chapter and those who have never regarded the books of the Ancients nor read a single letter of them.
And for this reason, this manner of the learned in our land is private; and I have not forgotten this at any time; and I have not adopted this except through long study of the books of the Ancients and study on the understanding of them, until I extracted the knowledge from them.
And then I applied it to experiment and study throughout my life.
And I have already described in this chapter all that my knowledge contains and on which my experiment is based; as I have abbreviated this for you and freed it from lengthy occupation; and I have abbreviated this to the end of abbreviation; and I have shown this at the end of clarification; and I have formed in this many forms of the instruments that are administered in it, as it is done by adding clarification, as I have done in the previous two chapters.
First chapter.
Summaries and collections of the nature of bone fractures, from those whose preface is necessary, before we begin the recollection of broken members and the diversity of each. Therefore, we must state in the preface of this chapter the summaries of the discourse; and the chapters to the understanding of which at the beginning the practitioners are forced and to dwell on the truth of them; that is, you and those who are eager to know or learn this noble art among you.
And thus I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or falling occurs, then you must hasten at the beginning with bloodletting or alleviating that, or both together, if no cause prohibits it, such as weakness of strength, or if it happens to a child, or an old person in decrepitude, or if it is a time of intense heat, or intense cold.
And then be content with a diet of fresh herbs and meat of birds and goats; and prohibit heavy meats and filling oneself with food and any food that fills the veins with blood, until you are assured of preventing abscess, and if you do not fear the effusion of material to the part.
And then return the patient to their previous regimen with which they are accustomed.
And thus when the broken bone begins to be restored, then the patient must be fed with nourishing food of substantial and heavy nutrition in which there is viscosity, such as foods made of wheat cooked with water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and bellies of cows, and eggs, and fresh fish, and thick wine and similar to them, and with this regimen, the coagulation of the fracture is made more easily and better.
And know that broken bones in people who are in their prime and in the decrepit, it is not possible for them to be continued and consolidated according to their nature due to the dryness of their parts.
But still nature joins and amends over the broken bone from all parts some substance similar to glue in which there is thickness that adheres and tightens it until they are glued together and bound together, until they come to the end of strength and firmness, just like fire at the beginning, until no cause prohibits it from its work.
And for this reason, it is necessary to provide the patient with food, food in which there is gravity and viscosity and thickness, as we have said.
And know that the types of fracture are diverse according to the diversity of the parts, for a fracture of the leg bone is different from a fracture of the head bone; and a fracture of the chest bone is different from a fracture of the back bone; and similarly, all other parts are different among them.
And I come with the recollection of every type of fracture, explained in its chapter distinct from the other.
Great diversity of fracture in itself. And the types of fracture of the bone are diversified in themselves; for there is an arched fracture different from what occurs in stars; and sometimes there is a fracture along the length of the bone: and these are fractures of splinters and splinters and protruding and non-protruding additions, just as is done in the pen when it is prepared for writing, and there is a fracture with a wound and disruption in the head, and there is a small fissure fracture.
And for each type, there is its own method or instrument in the restoration of it as will be remembered distinctly in its places.
Great signs of bone fracture. And by this is a bone fracture known: it is the tortuosity of it, and its prominence and appearance to the touch, and it is that when you compress it with your hand.
And thus when there is no apparent tortuosity in the place and it is not done by your touch when you touch the bone with movement and the patient does not find great pain, then there is no fracture here.
However, it is possible that there is tortuosity or a small fissure, then you must not harm it with your hand and with complete compression; then apply to it the medicines which will be remembered at the appropriate moment for the place; and then it should be tightened with a subtle constriction.
And know that the place when it is arched and not split in two or different from what does not happen in splinters, as every part of its counterpart is kept, then you must begin immediately to rectify it before it gets a hot abscess.
And if it gets a hot abscess, then leave it for a few days until the abscess ceases; and then straighten it in every way you can with lightness and skill.
And know that the restoration of it and the healing of it is easier than that of the bone in which splinters occur.
And then tighten it according to the remembrance of it.
But if there are splinters in the bone, then extension of the broken part from two sides is necessary, if it is the hand or the foot; or with your hand if the part is small; or with two ropes or with one rope and the hand.
And be your position with which you place the part equal according to its natural shape, while the parts of the broken part are extended, then you must return those additions with skill and in every way you can in their places.
And guard yourself according to your strength that no pain or injury happens to the patient by your operation; and force yourself according to your ability to apply one bone with the other its companion according to their best forms.
And it is necessary that at that time you skillfully touch it with your hand, and if you see any deviation, correct and align it according to your ability.
And strongly avoid excessive extension and compression, as many foolish doctors often cause a hot abscess by their operation, or cause contraction in the part, as we have seen happen many times by their operations.
And the quality of the constriction of the broken part is what I recount; so you know that broken parts are diverse in their smallness, greatness, and shape.
And for those that are small like the arm and the finger and the joint and similar to them, then the wrapping must be of very fine cloth.
But for those that are large like the thigh or the leg, they must be wrapped with broad and hard material, because the broad binding connects the large part and tightens it equally from all sides, so that no blemish enters.
And then begin, with your equable evacuation, to place a suitable binding on the site of the fracture with three or four wrappings as the part requires; and tighten your hand a little with the binding.
And then go with that to the upper part of the fracture site, and tighten less than the constriction with which you tightened the fracture site. And then extend the wrapping of the fracture site a little, and gradually loosen the constriction, until you take a large part from the site.
And then take another bandage and wrap it again over the broken site with wrapping, and then go with the wrappings to the lower part of the fracture; and let your operation be in the constriction of the wrapping and in the loosening of it as we have said in the first wrapping above.
